#### [Introduction to stored procedures](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-stored-procedures?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-stored-procedures?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Imagine you have a magic recipe that cooks a delicious dish. Stored procedures are like those recipes. Once created, anyone can use them by following the steps. It's like cooking the same testy meal without having to figure out the recipe each time. Another example, think of a chef who prepares a dish regularly. They get faster each time because they know the steps well. Similarly, when you use a stored procedure, the server figures out the best way to do the things first time. After that, it keeps a quick way to do it again. It's like having a chef who gets faster and more efficient with every cooking session. Stored procedures are prepared [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) code that you save so you can reuse it over and over again. So if you have any SQL query that you write over and over again, you can save it as a stored procedure and call it to run whenever needed. It's quite similar to the functions which you see in the programming world. Stored procedures are created to perform one or more [Data Manipulation](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Data%20Manipulation.md) operations on [Databases](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Databases.md). It is nothing but a group of SQL statement that accepts some input in the form of parameters
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-stored-procedures?u=76281980&t=97)** and perform some task and may or may not return a value. The advantages or the benefits of using the stored procedures are many. Let's understand some of them. Reusable, as I mentioned earlier as well, multiple users and multiple application can easily use and reuse stored procedure by just calling them, just like we do in normal programming functions. So you have a functions, you can call those functions again and again. Stored procedures are easy to modify. You can quickly change the statements in that procedures, and whenever you want to do this, you have the ALTER command through which you can go and change the stored procedure definition. Another interesting benefit which comes along with the procedure is the security. They enhance your database security. By controlling the access of the data, you're not directly exposing your tables or columns. What you are exposing, your procedure. If somebody wanted to play with your table, they have to just call your procedure, and you give the user an access for procedure level. Now procedure can change the table data as per the defined logic only, so you can secure your data
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-stored-procedures?u=76281980&t=190)** up to quite certain limit from getting corrupted from having the inconsistent value or some junk data. When a stored procedure is called, only the name of the procedure and the parameter needed to be sent over the network. Hence, it reduces the amount of data that needed to be transmitted over the network. This could result in improving the performance, especially in the scenarios where we have a very limited bandwidth. Procedures undergo a process that is called as query optimization. When they are first time executed, the database engine generates and store an optimal execution plan for these procedures. Subsequent invocations of the same procedure reuse this plan, leading to the faster execution times. The optimization contribute to the improved performance over time. In nutshell, stored procedures are the database objects that offer efficiency, security, and adaptability. They provide a level of abstraction, allowing developers to work with modular and reusable code, ensuring [Data Integrity](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Data%20Integrity.md) and optimization. Theory is done.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-stored-procedures?u=76281980&t=283)** Now it's time to jump to our pgAdmin and see how you can go and create your stored procedure. We're going to see this into the next video. Stay tuned.

### 8. Indexes and Performance

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [Introduction to indexes](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-indexes?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-indexes?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Imagine you have a vast library with thousands of the books. You want to find a specific book; for instance, "The Great Gatsby". Now, think of the library catalog as an index. Without the catalog, you might have to go through each shelf, check each book title, and waste a lot of time until you find the one which you want. If the library has an organized catalog, that the list of the books, along with the titles and the shelf numbers, it will make your lookup quite easy, because you can just reference that index and you can grab the book from a specific shelf. Or maybe take in another example, think of a restaurant menu. Without having any categories, now, it would be hard to find the dish which you're looking for. An index acts like a categorized menu, making it easy for the waiter to quickly locate and serve the dish you ordered. In [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md), an index do the exactly the same purpose. An index in database structure provides a quick and efficient way to look up and retrieve the data from a table. It works much like an index in a book,
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-indexes?u=76281980&t=96)** where you have a list of keywords, and each keywords point to the pages where you can find information related to that keyword. An index helps you to organize the data, accelerate the data retrieval, and improves the overall efficiency of searching for a specific information within a large dataset. It helps the database quickly pinpoint the desired information, making data retrieval faster and enhancing the [user experience](../../Skills/Web%20Development/User%20Experience%20(UX).md). Let's dive into the types of the indexes. There are variety of indexes. The single-column index: Sometimes, you create the index based on one column only. In those cases, the indexes are termed as single-column index. However, sometimes you might have a requirement where you want to make a combination of multiple columns to form an index. In that case, the index is termed as composite index. It is made up of two, or more than two, columns. Unique index: Ensure that an index column does not the duplicate values. So, if you have any column which you feel that contains a unique value, you probably try to create a unique index on it. Clustered index:
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-indexes?u=76281980&t=191)** This determines the physical order of the data rules in the table. Non-clustered index: This creates a separate structure for the index, and the table data remains are noted. Ideally, you should use an index on a column that is frequently used in your where-clause for filtering. You can also use the indexes on the column, which are very frequently involved in your joint operation. Or maybe you can try to create the index on the column which you use for your order-by, or a group-by clause. In nutshell, an index in a SQL acts as a performance optimization tool, which allows the database engine to quickly locate and retrieve specific data from a table, especially when dealing with a large data set. It plays a crucial role in enhancing the overall speed and efficiency of [Database Queries](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Database%20Queries.md). Let's deep dive into creating and managing these indexes in the next video.

We also need to monitor the performance. We can use the tools like explain to analyze the query plans and identify which indexes are being used effectively. Sometimes we need to balance between the reads and the writes. While indexes can dramatically improve the read operations, they can also slow down the write operations, like your insert, update, delete, because the indexes need to be updated. Select star retrieves all the columns, which is inefficient and sometimes, you don't need all those columns as well, and unnecessary people do select star. We are used to say select star from table and we leave this empty. We can put the limit as well. For example, in this above query, we are trying to pull out all the records and maybe I was just concerned with two records or three records only. I could have said it like limit two. So in this case, this will only pull out the two records, rather than the entire set of record. This would be very efficient way where the table size is too high and you might be just scanning the tables to get an idea what kind of a data it is there. In those cases, if you don't limit it, it will try to pull out all the rules, which will make this query works very slow. So keep in mind, whenever you're trying
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/basic-performance-tuning-techniques?u=76281980&t=284)** to retrieve the data, if you can minimize this retrieval, do that. Another ninja technique would be is optimize the subquery using the [CTE](../../Glossary/Concept/CTE.md). CTE stands for [common table expression](../../Glossary/Concept/CTE.md). Now, sometimes you use these subqueries, a query within a query, to get the result. Subqueries is not the right way. Subqueries makes the things work slow. So, whenever you encounter the subquery, instead of using the subquery, you can create the [CTEs](../../Glossary/Concept/CTE.md) or common table expression and then use that CTE to do the work. If you do this way, you're going to have the better performance. Optimization has multiple advantages. It's reduced the redundancy. Optimized query, eliminate the redundancy by fetching only the necessary things. For example, if your query is optimized, eventually it has a lower redundancy, it has, instead of all the columns, probably it'll pull out only the relevant columns. Instead of all the rows, it might be pulling only the relevant rows. Optimization also improves self readability. > **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/basic-performance-tuning-techniques?u=76281980&t=378)** Make it easier to understand and maintain. [Scalability](../../Skills/Artificial%20Intelligence%20(AI)/Scalability.md). The optimized query may scales better. As it separates the logic into the distinct parts, maybe in terms of a join using CTE, et cetera, this makes it more adaptable to the changes. #### [Introduction to database security](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-database-security?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-database-security?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Imagine your [PostgreSQL](../../Skills/Software%20Development/PostgreSQL.md) database as a secret vault where you store all your valuable information. Now just like you wouldn't want unauthorized people getting into your secret vault, you need to secure your PostgreSQL database to keep your data safe and sound. Or you can also assume your [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) database is like a VIP club and each user is a guest. You decide who gets an invitation. In technical terms, database security refers to implementation of measures and protocols to protect a database system, its data and its infrastructure from unauthorized access, misuse, and other potential threats. The primary objective of database security is to ensure the confidentiality, integrity, and availability of your data. Let's understand these objective in more detail. Confidentiality is kind of keeping your secret safe. In data terms, it means making sure only authorized people can access sensitive information like passwords or your private details. Confidentiality is like the lock on your bank wallet. Only you or the one to whom you trust
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-database-security?u=76281980&t=98)** have the key to access what's inside. In the digital world, it means safeguarding the personal information like credit card details, debit card details from your unauthorized eyes. Just as you wouldn't want someone snooping in your world, you don't want unauthorized access to sensitive data. Integrity is about trustworthiness of information. It is like ensuring that your data remains accurate and untampered. Imagine if your grades were changed in your school's database, that's an integrity concern. Availability is like your favorite streaming service, always ready to play your favorite show. If it suddenly went offline or took forever to load, that would be frustrating. In the data world, availability ensures that your information is accessible when you need it. For example, you want [E-Commerce](../../Skills/Web%20Development/E-Commerce.md) website to always load swiftly so customer can purchase data without delays or maybe you want to ensure that this website is available 24 across seven. Here are the benefits of the database security, protecting the sensitive information.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-database-security?u=76281980&t=193)** Database security shields personal and confidential data from unauthorized access. For example, imagine you are holding the sensitive data of the patient's health in the hospital. Now, you don't want this information to be shared to the outside world, or maybe we talk about the credentials information or the account details of the customers of the bank. You don't want all these to be exposed to outside people. Preventing unauthorized access, it ensures that only authorized user can enter the digital premises, preventing data breaches. For example, only admin should be allowed to go and see and change some information. However, there are people who is low into the hierarchy should not have an privilege to go and see the information or change the information. Maintaining [Data Integrity](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Data%20Integrity.md). Database security safeguards against tampering, deletion or corruption, preserving the accurate information. You don't want that if your password is stored in the database, it got changed automatically, or maybe somebody play with your personal information and change that, you don't want it. That is about keeping your data integrity. Ensuring the business continuity.
>
> **[4:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/introduction-to-database-security?u=76281980&t=288)** It prevents downtime, ensuring uninterrupted services and transaction. Meeting compliance requirement, database security ensures adherence to the legal and industry standard to avoid any penalties. There is a lot of data compliances needed to be taken care based on some country or geography. For example, if we talk about the European system, in the European countries, you will find that there is strict norms about the data, so database security helps you to comply to those compliances. Safeguarding against cyber threats. These database security measures acts as a digital security system, protecting against the hackers and malware. Let's deep dive into the database security in the SQL world and see how you can apply all this. See you into the next video.

#### [Understanding users and roles in SQL](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/understanding-users-and-roles-in-sql?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/understanding-users-and-roles-in-sql?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Users and roles are the key to controlling who gets in and what they can do in your [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) database. Imagine users are like individual employees, each with a unique digital identity, such as user IDs, your employee IDs like that. Meanwhile, roles are comparable to the project team, such as they're part of a sales team, marketing team, operations, et cetera. Just as you assign an employee to a project for efficient task management, similarly, in the SQL, you give roles to specific users. For example, to user one, you give the roles of a sales team. For user two, you might give roles of admin. In SQL, a user is a distinct entity that can connect to a database. User have individual identities and credential for authentication. For example, when you have an employee in your team, it has its own user ID and password to log into the database, right? That could be a user. In SQL, a role is a named group of privileges that can be assigned to the user. Sometimes, instead of giving different permissions to different people, you can create the roles and what roles can do
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/understanding-users-and-roles-in-sql?u=76281980&t=93)** is roles you create based on a reader, a writer, or an admin, or those kind of way you can create the roles and then you can assign these type of roles to a user. So then a user can become a reader, a user have the writing privileges or user might have the admin privileges like that. By assigning users the roles, you can efficiently manage the access control. Changes to the role privileges automatically applies to all the associate users. For example, imagine that there are 10 people who has a role as an admin. Now, if you change the access control of this admin level, then all the 10 people access control will get changed. Let's understand the benefits of creating users and assigning role in context to the database. The granular access control. If you have users and roles, then you can have a very granular level of access to the [Databases](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Databases.md). You can give a very specific permission to a specific user, what he can do and what he cannot. So this can add another layer of security to your database. Streamlined privilege management. Instead of adjusting access for each person, what we're going to do is you can assign the roles to each people
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/understanding-users-and-roles-in-sql?u=76281980&t=189)** and you can give the permission at the role level so that if at any point of a time you want to update these permissions or privileges, you can do through the role itself. You don't have to separately do it for every user. Simplified user administration. User and roles make it easy to add new user or change access for a group, keeping [User Management](../../Skills/Web%20Development/User%20Management.md) pretty straightforward. It also helps to enhance the security. How? Users and roles make sure only the right people can access the sensitive data. It's not only about having the username and password, even if the user has the correct username and password, but if it does not have the correct permissions, he cannot still see the data. So users and role can help to enhance the security to next level. It also helps to improve the maintenance. With users and roles, tasks like updating access rules or removing privileges becomes simpler, making database maintenance much smoother. We already talked too much. Now it's time to go and see the technical implementation of it, how you can create the users and how you can assign the roles. In the next video, we're going to talk about the same. Stay tuned.

#### [Granting and revoking permissions](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/granting-and-revoking-permissions?u=76281980)

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/granting-and-revoking-permissions?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Granting permissions are like giving keys to specific doors in a building while revoking the permissions is like taking back the keys from someone who no longer needs access. In [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md), permissions control what action users or role can perform on specific database objects. There are multiple types of permissions available in the SQL world. Let's see some of them and understand what are these permissions. Select. The Select permission allows someone to run the select query. It allows you to read the data from a specific table or a specific view. Insert permissions grants the ability to add new rules to a table. Let's say if you want to add new rules to a table, you need to have that insert permission available on that table for your role. Update. As the name suggest update is the permission which helps you to change any specific row within a table. If you want to change a specific column value, you'll need to have an update privileges attached to your role. Delete. Delete allows the removal of rules from a table. If you feel that there are some rules which you want
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/granting-and-revoking-permissions?u=76281980&t=96)** to remove from the table, you can only do it if you have this delete permission. Execute. Execute permission helps you to execute these stored procedure. If you are running any SQL query, which is having an stored process execution needed, then you can only execute that query if you have the execute permission. Connect. it helps you to connect to a database. If you don't have the correct permission on your role, you cannot connect to a database. Create. Create grants the ability to create new objects within a database or a schema such as your tables, Temporary or Temp. That allows you to create the temporary tables within a session. Now you understand the variety of permission options available in the SQL. #### [Using roles for permission management](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/using-roles-for-permission-management?u=76281980)

#### [Best practices for managing roles and permissions](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980&t=0)** - Managing rules and permission in [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md), or any database system, is critical for ensuring database security, maintaining efficient access control, and ensuring that user have the appropriate level of access needed for their task. Here are some detailed best practices for managing roles and permissions. Principle of least privileges. This ensures that the users and roles have only the minimum level of access necessary to perform their function. For example, imagine that you have one team member. Now this team member only look for the customer problems and look at the customer data. Then you should only grant the customer table permissions to this person. You should not give him the permission to do something on the product, or on order data, because this person is not dealing with those tables. This is how you can implement the least privileges. You try to give only the lowest level of access to every person. Another best practice would be the role hierarchies. Role hierarchies involve creating roles with a specific set of permissions, and then assigning these roles to other roles or users.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980&t=97)** This effectively grouping permissions into manageable units. Remember our previous example we created the sales team. Now we have the sales manager, which is having the same hierarchy, right? So based on your organizational hierarchy, you can similarly create the rule hierarchies. This will separate out who is getting what kind of an access. So this is also very popular based practice mechanism where your actual role is quite similar to your organizational roles. Another best practice would be use a schema-based access control. Sometimes instead of putting all your tables into a one common schema, like we have done it under the public schema, in our examples, we can create these separate schemas. We can say that there is a one customer schema, one product schema, one order schema. Now you might have a multiple tables related to customer like customer address, customer liking, customer feedbacks. You can keep all those customer data under the customer schema. Similarly, all product related multiple tables, you keep it under the product schema, and then you can assign the users access at the schema level. This will ensure that they are not interfering
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980&t=192)** into someone else table, and that will keep the things quite secure. Another best practice would be is doing regular audits and review. Ideally, every team should periodically review the rules and permissions, and ensure that the rule assignments are up to the date with the current policies and user responsibilities. They should also scrutiny and check is there any deviation or if they find any inconsistency in the privileges granted to specific roles or the users. Segregation of duties is also one of the best practices where you divide the responsibilities among the different roles and users to reduce the risk of unauthorized access for any kind of fraudulent activities. For example, you have a separate rules for a data entry team and data approval can prevent unauthorized data modification. Another best practice would be using the NOINHERIT. Now this NOINHERIT attribute prevents the role from automatically inheriting the permissions from the roles it is member of. Users must explicitly set their role to one they are member of to use its permissions. Limit superuser role usage.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980&t=290)** You remember what superuser do? Superuser permission will grant you the full access that this user can do anything. Now, the moment you give someone a super user, you are breaking the least privilege rule. So ideally you should limit while giving the super user role to someone. You don't want everyone to have the full access. This could have a significant [Security Risk](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Security%20Risk.md). Utilize application-specific roles. Sometimes it's not just a user who is connecting to your database. Maybe you have a website, you have a mobile application, you have another desktop based application. Those application directly connecting to the database to get or push the information. In that case, you should have a specific role assigned to them because this is something of a programmatic way. You give them only the least privilege based access control. You can also think of using the data encryption and data masking. Sometimes when you store the PII, that is personal identification information like account numbers, card details, or some medical data, probably you can use the masking where every user cannot see that data directly. By following these best practices,
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/best-practices-for-managing-roles-and-permissions?u=76281980&t=388)** you can create a robust security model for your post grade SQL database that protects sensitive data, ensures users have appropriate access level, and helps maintaining the integrity and confidentiality of your database environment. After securing the database, now it's time to understand what can go wrong in your database and how we can recover from that. So in the next video we are going to talk about the basic common errors which can come in the SQL or database world and how you can get rid of them. See you there.

Similarly, understanding SQL syntax error is crucial for anyone working with the database as these are the common mistakes or issues, which arises when you write and execute SQL queries. Syntax error occur when the SQL statement does not conform to the rules of the SQL language grammar. These error can prevent your SQL statement from executing. Let's just look at some of the common SQL errors, which can come and how we can solve them. Many times, SQL error comes something like this. I am selecting the rules from customer table. #### [Logical errors in SQL](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Logical error in [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) are mistakes that happen when your instruction to the database don't achieve what you intended. It's like telling someone to make a sandwich, but instead of putting the peanut butter and jelly together, they put peanut butter and the mayonnaise. Their steps may be correct, but the result is not what you wanted. Logical errors in SQL refers to mistakes or flaws in the logic of SQL query that lead to unintended results. Unlike syntax errors which are caught by the SQL parser and prevent the query from executing, logical errors allows the query to run, but the result is incorrect, and it is not what you are expecting out of the query. These kind of errors sometimes is more challenging to identify and resolve because they often requires a deep understanding of both the data and the problem statement that you're trying to solve. Let's talk about some common types of logical errors in SQL and strategies to address them, Incorrect join. You might find that logical error can occur when the JOIN condition between the tables is incorrect or maybe the wrong type of join is used.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980&t=94)** For example, instead of using the LEFT JOIN, you might have used the RIGHT OUTER JOIN, so sometimes using the incorrect join, putting the wrong condition, could be the reason of your logical error. To solve this problem, you can review the JOIN conditions and ensure that you're using the correct type of the join and correct condition as per the problem statement. Another reason could be is misuse of aggregate function. Aggregating data incorrectly can lead to logical error. For an example, including non-aggregated column in the SELECT without including them in the GROUP BY could be a problem. For example, you are trying to do the sum, average, or count. Another reason of logical error could be using incorrect WHERE and HAVING clause. You need to be very clear that WHERE clause should be used before the GROUP BY condition. If you use the WHERE clause incorrectly, that can filter out the rules in an unexpected manner. If you have some GROUP BY or aggregated values and you are trying to filtering it out, then you have to use the HAVING after the GROUP BY only. So a proper knowledge of the WHERE and HAVING clause is needed to get the correct filtered data. Incorrect subquery can also be another reason
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980&t=188)** of your logical errors. A lot of times when you have a complex requirement, you tend to use the subqueries, which is a query inside a query. If the output of these subqueries are not properly formatted, probably this could create some kind of a logical problem. So ensure that if your query has some logical errors, and if it is having a subqueries, check that subquery portion as well. Handling NULL values could be one of our biggest problem of the logical error. Sometimes you misunderstood the NULL with 0 or some default value. NULL is actually representing unknown or missing values. If you are doing any comparison along with the NULL, ensure that NULL comparison will never comes out to be the true because NULL is always something which is unknown. So if you have done any of the condition based on the NULL, you need to ensure that you are using proper NULL handling, like using IS NULL, IS NOT NULL, or the functions like COALESCE or NVL. Assuming [Data Integrity](../../Skills/Cybersecurity/Data%20Integrity.md) without considering the impact of the constraint, like foreign key, unique key, or some constraint, can also lead to the problem of logical errors. So you need to ensure that whatever be the primary key, foreign key, or unique key
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980&t=282)** that you are assuming is exactly like that as per the schema also. Many times, you use the UNION, INTERSECT and ACCEPT. These are called as generally the set operations. If you are using these kind of a set operations into the query, this could also result into some kind of a logical errors if they have not been implemented in the right way. So if these are also involved in your query, ensure that you are using them correctly. and you have a proper understanding of how to use these set operations. Let's talk about the strategies which you can apply to identify and resolve these kind of a logical error. The first and foremost thing which you can do is review and test. Ideally, you should break down your complex query into smaller parts as far as possible. Review each part individually and then test with known dataset to verify its correctness. Many times, many projects employ this best practice of doing the peer review. You write one piece of a query, and then you have your teammate who is going to review this piece of query so that the fresh piece of eyes when see your code, probably they might see some errors. You can also use SQL linkers and formatters. They help you to make your queries more readable,
>
> **[6:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/logical-errors-in-sql?u=76281980&t=377)** and once your query is more readable, sometimes it is easy to catch those logical errors. Data and requirement cross-verification. Sometimes you don't know what kind of data is available in the table, and you are also not very sure about the requirement. So sometimes if you understand the requirement properly, and you do the cross-verification, that will help you to resolve those logical errors because sometimes the problem is not in your query. The problem could be in your understanding of the requirement. If you understand the requirement properly, probably you can put the logic accordingly into your query and get the expected output. Logical error requires a thorough understanding of both the SQL knowledge and the specific database schema on which you are working. Addressing these errors often involves careful review, testing, and sometimes rethinking the approach to query the data. In the next video, we're going to talk about the debugging skills in SQL. See you there.

> [!transcript]- Transcript

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/debugging-null-values?u=76281980&t=0)** - [INstructor] Debugging null values in [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) is a crucial aspect of [Database Management](../../Topics/Database%20Management.md). It is important because null represent the absence of a value in a column. Null is not same as empty string or zero. It signifies unknown or not applicable. Misunderstanding or mishandling of null values can relate to unexpected results or logical errors in your SQL queries. Let's go back to over PG admin and see how we can handle the null values. Let's say I want to find out all the [products](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Microsoft%20Products.md) for which the price is null. If I say something like that, select start from products where price equal to null and I do this. This will not going to work because you cannot compare null with the null. Null is a kind of unknown. You cannot say one unknown is equal to another unknown. If you do this, you will not get any result, but if you say something like this, where price is null and then you execute, you see the two result where price column is null. So whenever you are comparing the null, you should use a function called is null or if you don't want a null values,
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/debugging-null-values?u=76281980&t=93)** you should say is not null. This will give you all the records where that column is not null or else sometimes you do the logical operator, you say like one condition is null, another condition is something else. Similarly, when you do the logical comparison of two conditions, in that case also you need to be very careful when using the null. For example, if I say select true and null. So if true and true ideally should give true. But when you have a one condition coming out as true and other condition is null, your output will still going to come as null. Reason is null is consider as unknown. So even when you are doing just like a direct checking or you are using some kind of a conditional, and, or, or these kind of a logical operator, every time you have to be careful that if you are dealing with the nulls, nulls cannot compare directly. You have to use isnull, isnotnull like that. You also need to be very careful that when you are using the aggregate functions. So the functions like average, max, min, all these function does not include the null values. They exclude the null, but the aggregate function like count star.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/debugging-null-values?u=76281980&t=187)** This is something which going to include the null values as well. So remember, except count function, all the aggregate function does not consider the null but count function consider the null as well. Let's talk about some of the common debugging scenarios. For example, unexpected empty results set. A common issue is when queries written empty sets because the query condition involves comparison within null values. For instance, filtering a data set with column equal to null will not yield any result as we have seen in the previous example. Similarly, sometimes an incorrect aggregation could also be a problem because you have not considered that max, min, sum, average will not count your null values. However, your count will count in the null values as well. Another could be is join condition. When you join two tables and if one of the join key has null values, in that case, the rows with null in both the tables will not going to match. You cannot say that null of this one table could match with the null of another table. This could potentially leading to a fever join results than what you anticipated. To sort out this null problem, there is some debugging strategies which you can think of.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/debugging-null-values?u=76281980&t=283)** For example, using is null or is not null. This example we have already seen. Another one is using COALESCE. COALESCE function handle the null values by providing an alternative value. In the COALESCE function, you can pass some default value. If this column is having a null value instead of coming the null, it'll give you that default value. You can think of using the NULLIF functions that will return null if two expressions are equal. You can also have the conditional aggregation. When you aggregate the data, consider whether you need to count null values or treat them differently. Outer joins, if you need to include rows that have a null values in the join key, consider using the outer joins like left join, right join, or full outer join. When working with the data that can contain null values, you can include a specific test to ensure that query logic correctly handles these cases. Ideally, you should do proper testing and validation. In a complex queries involving multiple handling of null values, documentation and comment can help someone to understand the query in much easier way and it'll make your code more maintainable. By carefully considering,
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/debugging-null-values?u=76281980&t=379)** how null values are handled in your SQL queries and employing appropriate functions and condition to manage them, you can avoid common pitfalls and ensure that query returns the expected results. So this could be the reason that when we are seeing our monthly report, we see two specific rows coming out to be null, and that's why our total sales quantity is coming null. And the reason of this total sales quantity null or less is because for some of the product, our system has a wrong price. Ideally, you should not have a zero price for any product. Got it? So we can go back and we can put down the correct price for these product and then our analysis will come perfectly fine. We could just go down and say that update products table, and we can set some price, let's say the price =100 where my product_id =1.
>
> **[5:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/practical-example-debugging-real-sql-issues?u=76281980&t=322)** And similarly, let me do it for product_id for the price is 200. Let me just execute this. And then if we just go down and see our monthly report, we will get the specific amounts. Got it? So that's how you can sometimes go back and analyze in your real world what could be the problem. Go step by step and check each and every line and identify where it could be possibly the problem is. So we have extensively covered what could be the problems which we can face while writing the SQL queries. And by now, you got the understanding how you can get rid of those errors. In the next video, we're going to talk about the next level in the SQL world, that is the ETL. See you there.

### 11. ETL Overview

[↑ Back to Table of Contents](#table-of-contents)

#### [What is ETL and its importance](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Lecturer] ETL stands for extract, transform, and load. This concept is at the heart of [Data Warehousing](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Data%20Warehousing.md), [business intelligence](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Business%20Intelligence%20(BI).md) and [Data Integration](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Data%20Integration.md) strategies across the industries. Today let's explore what ETL is and why it's crucial and how it empowers businesses to make informed decisions. ETL is a three step process used in the [Database Management](../../Topics/Database%20Management.md) systems and data warehousing world. Let's understand each one of them. Extract. The first steps involve extracting the data from variety of sources. These sources can range from RDBMS system. It could be CRM system. It could be CSV file, [JSON](../../Skills/Web%20Development/JSON.md) file. It could be SFTP. It could be FTP. It could be any data source possible. The goal here is to gather all the necessary data from these data sources regardless of the format or the type of data source. Now the transformation, which is the second step where we try to transform the data which we have extracted in the step one. This stage is all about turning raw data into something meaningful.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980&t=96)** You try to do this transformation like you remove the null values. You might remove the duplicate, you remove the outliers, you put on the business rules, you do some kind of a validation check, and then you transform the data which is in more digestible form, which is more accurate, and help to solve some kind of a business problem. The third step is load. The final step is loading this transformed data into the target system, which is in general, most of the time you will find it as a data warehousing solution. So the idea is you pull the data from your data sources. That could be generally your old TP [Databases](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Databases.md) or CRM system or those kind of different sources. You extract, you transform, and then you load it into data warehousing, all the OLAP systems. And later on, the data analyst, your BI team or your [SQL](../../Skills/Data%20Science/SQL.md) analyst folks will query this data warehouse to get some meaningful information. Let's understand the importance of the ETL process. ETL is more than just a [Data Processing](../../Skills/Database%20Management/Data%20Processing.md) pipeline. It is a foundational component
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980&t=189)** for effective [Data Management](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Data%20Management.md). It is important for data consolidation. ETL allows businesses to consolidate the data from multiple sources into a single coherent repository. This helps you to form a unified view, which is sometimes very important when you are doing the comprehensive analysis and reporting. ETL is important to improve the [Data Quality](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Data%20Quality.md) as well. The transformational step in the ETL world try to make your data more cleaner and more meaningful to the business. It tries to do all sort of validations, applying business rules and clean the data. That's why ETL process helps to improve the data quality. ETL process is many times is very automatic and repetitive. So if some process runs automated way, it can save a lot of time. You can set the ETL process which can run at a fixed defined frequency, maybe every hour, every minute, every once in a day, like that. ETL process also helps in the historical data management. This process enables businesses
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980&t=283)** to store historical data very efficiently. This is historical perspective is important when you are doing some kind of a trend analysis or [Forecasting](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Forecasting.md) or you might be doing some strategic planning. ETL process are common across multiple industries. In the real world, if we talk about the retail industry there also ETL is very popular. ETL can integrate your customer, sales, inventory and all variety of your operational data to provide insights into the customer behavior and supply chain efficiency. ETL can be very useful in the financial institutions as well, where you can have consolidated transaction data from multiple system which help for the fraud detection or maybe from compliance reporting purpose. In healthcare domain ETL process can merge patients record from variety of systems, improving, care coordination and patient's outcome. To sum up, ETL is a critical process for any data-driven organization. It enables efficient, accurate and timely use of data and helps the business to take the informed decision based on that data.
>
> **[6:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/what-is-etl-its-importance?u=76281980&t=380)** Stay tuned for our next video where we will keep dive into ETL process flow. See you there.

#### [ETL process flow](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/etl-process-flow?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/etl-process-flow?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In the last video, you understood the concept of ETL. Now it's time to get into ETL process flow and understand each stage in a little more detail. Let's start that. Our first stop is the extraction stage. That is called extract. This is the stage where data is gathered from variety of data sources. These data sources could be of any type, and it could be of any format. For example, the data could be the relational data from the RDBMS [Databases](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Databases.md) or the data source could be something like a file type, where the data might be in CSV, [JSON](../../Skills/Web%20Development/JSON.md), Parquet or any other file format. The primary goal here is to accurately and efficiently extract the required data without compromising its integrity. Extraction could be of multiple type. It could be either full extraction, where sometimes we call it like a full load, where we try to extract the full data, that is, the entire table, entire file, or entire database. Sometimes the extraction could be of an incremental one. In the incremental extraction, we retrieve only the latest data, or sometimes we call it like the delta portion, only the new records or the new data,
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/etl-process-flow?u=76281980&t=95)** which is came after our last pull. The next stage is the transformation stage. This is the stage where your raw data undergoes a specific type of metamorphosis to become more meaningful and actionable. This stage is where the heavy lifting occurs. This involves a lot of types of operation. For example, the cleaning. You try to clear out all the unwanted data. Maybe you filter out couple of rows, you may be removing all unwanted columns, you may be removing null values, you may be removing duplicate values, like that. A lot of normalization or standardization can also occur at this stage. Where you try to bring in disparate data formats into a harmony, trying to make your data more consistent across the data sets. You try to do the augmentation of data with additional insights. That is like you're trying to do the enrichment of more information by having the data from other external data sources. Here, you also try to aggregate the data so that it helps you to form the summarized detail of your large dataset. Maybe in this step,
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/etl-process-flow?u=76281980&t=187)** you also trying to do the validation as well, based on some business rules and constraints. Overall, this stage is tailor the data to fit the analytical or your operational need of the business to ensure that the data you have would be useful for insightful analysis. The last stage in this ETL journey is the load stage. This is the stage where exactly your data get dumped or copied into the destination data source. Or we call it, you load your transformed data into the target data source. Now, when you try to do this loading of data into the target data source, it could also be of a variety type. It could also be of a batch loading, or it could be kind of a [Real-Time](../../Skills/Database%20Management/Real-Time.md) loading. The batch loading is where data is loaded in a batches at a scheduled intervals. Maybe this is quite suitable for a non-time sensitive data. This method is efficient, but can result in data being slightly outdated. However, the real-time loading is the type of load where data is loaded continuously as it is become available. This approach is ideal for time-sensitive applications, but requires more robust system and infrastructure.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/etl-process-flow?u=76281980&t=285)** The choice between the batch and the real-time loading depends upon your specific need of the business or how much balance you want to make between your resource utilization. To summarize, ETL process flow is a carefully choreographed dance that transforms raw data into a structured, meaningful format, which is ready for analysis. Now, you must be thinking, how you can apply this ETL? What are the different tools out there? In the next video, we are going to talk about the variety of ETL tools. Stay tuned.

#### [Common ETL tools](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980&t=0)** - It's time to explore the ETL tools. These tools are the workhorses that automate and manage the extract, transform and load cycle, making the data more accessible and useful for the business. ETL tools are software applications, which is designed to facilitate the ETL process. It helps to extract data from variety of sources, helps to transforming it according to the business tools and requirement and helps to loading it into a destination, like a data warehouse for analysis. The choice of a ETL tools can significantly impact the efficiency of your data operations, the [Scalability](../../Skills/Artificial%20Intelligence%20(AI)/Scalability.md) of data process, and ultimately the insights which you can derive from the data. If you talk there are broadly, ETL tools can be divided into three categories. The first one is traditional on premises tools. Now, as the name suggests, these are the little older ones and mostly works at on premises environment. These are something which is installed and run on your organization [Hardware](../../Topics/Hardware.md). They offer some robust features but may require some significant
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980&t=94)** upfront investment and maintenance. Second type of ETL tool category could be is cloud-based tools. There are a lot of cloud-based ETL tools, which is quite popular these days and the advantage which come along with these cloud-based tools, is the scalability and the flexibility. Another important thing is it does not require a huge investment because most of these cloud-based ETL tools are pay-as-you go pricing, which helps you to start at a low cost itself. Another category is open source tool. Open source ETL tools are highly customizable and very cost effective also. They are supported by the communities of developers, but they require some more in-house expertise to manage. Now this might confuse you that which specific type of ETL tool you should choose. So to sort out this problem of choosing the right ETL tool, let's understand what specific features you should look for. The first and foremost feature is connectivity to diverse data source. Through ETL tools, you try to move the data from your one data source to another data source. The most important thing you need in your ETL tool
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980&t=192)** is the connectivity option available for your choice of data sources. For example, if you are trying to move the data from Dynamic 365 or [SQL server](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Microsoft%20SQL%20Server.md) and you try to store the data into [Azure](../../Skills/Cloud%20Computing/Microsoft%20Azure.md) Data Lake storage, or maybe you want to store this data in some SFTP server or FTP server, ideally you should choose an ETL tool which provides the connectivity to all these source and destination data source. Another important feature you probably need is transformation capability. You may doing a more complex transformation, so you should choose an ETL tool which provide all those kind of transformations you are looking for. Another good feature you are looking for is user friendliness. There are a lot of ETL tools available in the market, which is having a very good graphical user interface that makes the learning and doing very easy and fun. In the ETL world, many times you deal with a very huge data set, hence your ETL tool would be of such a quality that it has the scalability and the performance options. As your data size grows, this ETL tool should be smart enough to handle that huge load and still performs better.
>
> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980&t=285)** [Data Quality](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Data%20Quality.md) feature is also the something which you should look for because you have to manage your data quality. And if you have a ETL tool which support this along with the monitoring and logging, that will make your life much easier. Let's talk about some of the common popular ETL tools. The first one is Informatica PowerCenter. Informatica PowerCenter is a robust traditional ETL tool, which is known for its extensive features and it is very popular for strong [Data Integration](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Data%20Integration.md) capabilities. Another tool is Talend. Talend offers both open source and commercial version. This is also popular for flexible and allows broader connectivity option with variety of data sources. AWS Glue, this is fully managed, cloud-based ETL service that makes it easy to prepare and load data for analytics. Similar to the AWS Glue, you also have an Azure Data Factory ETL tool, which is coming from the [Microsoft Azure](../../Skills/Cloud%20Computing/Microsoft%20Azure.md) Cloud. This is also a fully managed cloud-based ETL service and it has a very smooth integration with lots of data sources and Azure ecosystem. In the [Google Cloud](../../Skills/Software%20Development/Google%20Cloud%20Platform%20(GCP).md),
>
> **[6:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/common-etl-tools?u=76281980&t=380)** you have the Google Cloud Dataflow ETL service. It is also a type of cloud service, which is managed service for stream and [Batch Processing](../../Skills/Data%20Science/Batch%20Processing.md). This seamlessly integrate with all the variety of Google Cloud services and ecosystem. There is one more tool that is Apache NiFi. It is an open source tool, which is designed for automated data flow management with user-friendly web UI. Each of these tool has its strengths and best choice, depends upon your specific data requirement, infrastructure, and budget. In conclusion, the right ETL tool can streamline your data processes, enhance data quality, and unlock valuable insights. Consider your organization's unique need and complexity of your data. You can choose the ETL tool which fits best for you.

>
> **[7:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/capstone-project-solution-insurance-claims-analysis?u=76281980&t=473)** because we just want on the monthly basis. So we say Date_Trunk it to the month, right? And we want claim frequency that is total number of claim count, so we say COUNT(*). And we also need the average claim amount, so I said AVG(ClaimAmount). Now, all these we are doing based on every month, right? So that's why we say GROUP BY this ClaimMonth. And that's it. If I execute this, I will get the claim month. And based on that claim month, I get the claim frequency and average claim amount. So it is saying that for the June month, we got one, for the July month, August, September, and October, we got one, one, one for each. If you put more it up, probably you will see little different frequency here. But that's how you can calculate the monthly claim frequency and average claim amount. Coming to the next task of this project, it was about the optimization. It is about how you can create the indexes or how we can improve the performance. So always remember, whenever you try to create the indexes, it should be created on the column,
>
> **[9:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/capstone-project-solution-insurance-claims-analysis?u=76281980&t=571)** which is more frequently expected to come in your queries. So far, we have not executed many queries, but in general, your date column could be a very good fit where you can create index. Because lot of time when you do a claim analysis in your insurance domain, you do many things based on the date, right? So date column could be a right fit here to have an index on it. How you can create the index, you can create the index using CREATE INDEX and then you give index name on a specific table and the column name. Just execute that. This will create the index on claim date column of Claims table. Now, going forward, whenever you write any query on Claims table, which is filtering based on claim date, you will have a better performance. Last task was about the rules and permission. It is more or less about your database security. It has been asked to create two roles, claim analyst and claims manager. Claim analyst is the role which just have only the read permissions on claim and policy data. Claims manager is someone who has the read as well as the full access,
>
> **[11:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/capstone-project-solution-insurance-claims-analysis?u=76281980&t=667)** that is update, delete, insert ability on your claim and policy data. How we can do that. You can create the role using CREATE ROLE ClaimsAnalyst, and you will say LOGIN capability with having PASSWORD sub, password1. Let's execute that. Similarly, you can create the claims manager using CREATE ROLE ClaimsManager, and then you have a login password and you can execute this. Now, so far we just created the role. Now, it's time to give them the permissions. How you can give them the permission. For ClaimsAnalyst, I just only want select permission, all the read-only permission. So I set GRANT SELECT ON Claims, Policy, PolicyType to ClaimAnalyst. And for the ClaimsManager, we want full access. So I said SELECT, INSERT, UPDATE, DELETE on these tables to ClaimManager. Let's execute. So that's how we have added the multiple roles along with the variety of privileges to these roles. You can also do a lot of more analysis in this project. Maybe you can add few more roles,
>
> **[12:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/complete-guide-to-sql-for-data-engineering-from-beginner-to-advanced/capstone-project-solution-insurance-claims-analysis?u=76281980&t=761)** you can create hierarchy, you can create views, you can create more analytical queries. All this you can do on your own as well.
